الخلاف في زيادة الإيمان ونقصه
٢١ - وَرُجِّحَتْ زِيَادَةُ الْإِيمَانِ بِمَا تَزِيدُ طَاعَةُ الْإِنْسَانِ
٢٢ - وَنَقْصُهُ بِنَقْصِهَا وَقِيلَ: لَا وَقِيلَ: لَا خُلْفَ كَذَا قَدْ نُقِلَا

قوله: (وَرُجِّحَتْ زِيَادَةُ الْإِيمَانِ ... إلخ): تقدَّمَ أن العمل من كمال الإيمان عند أهل السنة، وقد ذكر المصنف هنا أنه يزيد بزيادته وينقصُ بنقصه، فقال: (وَرُجِّحَتْ زِيَادَةُ الْإِيمَانِ ... إلى آخره؛ أي: رَجَّحَ جماعةٌ من العلماء وهم جمهورُ الأشاعرة القول بزيادة الإيمان؛ لأنه لا معنى لترجيح زيادة الإيمان إلا ترجيح القول بها. وقوله: بِمَا تَزِيدُ طَاعَةُ الْإِنْسَانِ أي: بسبب زيادة طاعة الإنسان، فالباء سببية، و(ما) مصدرية، والطاعةُ: فعلُ المأمور به، واجتناب المنهي عنه.
[The chapter on] the disagreement over the increase and decrease of faith. 21 - And the increase of faith is given preponderance by what the obedience of man increases. 22 - And its decrease by its decrease, and it was said: no, and it was said: no disagreement, thus it has been transmitted. His saying: 'And the increase of faith is given preponderance... etc.': It has preceded that action is from the perfection of faith according to Ahl al-Sunnah, and the author mentioned here that it increases by its increase and decreases by its decrease. So he said: 'And the increase of faith is given preponderance... to the end; meaning: a group of scholars, who are the majority of the Ash'aris, gave preponderance to the statement that faith increases; because there is no meaning to giving preponderance to the increase of faith except giving preponderance to the statement of it. And His saying: 'by what the obedience of man increases' means: due to the increase of man's obedience; so the ba' is causative, and 'ma' is masdariyya, and obedience is: doing what is commanded and refraining from what is forbidden.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage addresses a major theological issue: whether faith can increase and decrease. The commentator begins by quoting two lines from the matn (the poem) which state that the preponderant view is that faith increases when obedience increases and decreases when obedience decreases, and that some say there is no change, but the transmitted view is that there is no real disagreement (i.e., the difference is terminological). The commentator then explains that, according to Ahl al-Sunnah, actions are part of the perfection of faith. The author of the matn indicates that faith increases with obedience and decreases with sin, and a group of scholars (the majority of Ash'aris) have given preponderance to the view that faith actually increases, because speaking of 'increase of faith' only makes sense if faith can increase. He then analyzes the phrase 'by what the obedience of man increases' (bima tazidu ta'atu al-insani): the letter ba' is sababiyya (causative) and 'ma' is masdariyya (making the phrase a verbal noun), so the meaning is 'due to the increase of man's obedience'. Obedience itself is defined as doing what is commanded and avoiding what is forbidden.

Key Terms
إيمان
زيادة
نقص
طاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Ash'ari view reduces faith to mere actions, disregarding belief.
Correction: The Ash'aris maintain that faith includes both belief and actions; actions increase the perfection of faith, not its essence.

Checkpoint

A) By increase of knowledge only.
B) By increase of obedience.
C) By increase of wealth.
D) By acquisition of new beliefs.

Key Takeaway
Faith increases with obedience and decreases with disobedience, according to the majority of Ash'aris.

The Increase and Decrease of Faith (Iman)
Commentator explains increase and decrease of iman based on obedience and divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to the majority of Ash'aris, faith (iman) increases with obedience and decreases with disobedience, and that this change is ultimately under Allah's will.

Core Idea
Faith grows with obedience and shrinks with disobedience.

In this passage, the commentator explains the well-known Ash'ari position on the increase and decrease of iman. He clarifies that actions are part of the perfection of faith, so obedience increases faith and disobedience decreases it. However, he also notes that Allah may increase or decrease faith by His sheer will without any cause. This lesson covers the general principle and its grounding in the poem.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the first lines of the poem and commentary to see that the increase of faith is preponderated by increased obedience. Note that the 'ba' in 'bima tazidu' is causative. Ask: what does this imply about the relationship between faith and actions?
The commentator stresses that this is the view of the majority of Ash'aris.
2
Understand the nuances
Notice that the commentator adds that Allah may increase or decrease faith without any cause. This balances human agency with divine omnipotence. Reflect on why this nuance matters.
The text says: 'وإلا فقد يزيده المولى وينقصه بمحض اختياره من غير سبب يقتضيه'.
3
Apply the principle
Consider how this principle applies to ordinary believers. Then ask: does it apply to prophets and angels? This prepares for the next lesson.
The text transitions to limit the scope: 'فمحله في غير إيمان الأنبياء والملائكة'.

On the disagreement concerning the increase and decrease of faith. 21 - And the increase of faith is preponderated by what? – He said: by the increase of human obedience. 22 - And its decrease by its decrease. And it is said: no, and it is said: no disagreement, thus it has been transmitted. His saying: 'And the increase of faith is preponderated... etc.': It has preceded that action is from the perfection of faith according to Ahl al-Sunnah. And the author mentioned here that it increases with its increase and decreases with its decrease. So he said: (And the increase of faith is preponderated... to the end); meaning: a group of scholars, namely the majority of Ash'aris, preponderated the statement that faith increases; because there is no meaning to preponderating the increase of faith except preponderating the statement of it. And his saying: 'by what the obedience of man increases' means: due to the increase of human obedience, so the 'ba' is causative and 'ma' is masdariyya. And obedience is: doing what is commanded and avoiding what is forbidden. And his saying: 'and its decrease by its decrease' means: and the aforementioned group preponderated the statement of the decrease of faith due to the decrease of obedience. This is with respect to the matter, otherwise Allah may increase it and decrease it by His mere choice without any cause that necessitates it. And if we say that faith increases and decreases, its place is other than the faith of prophets and angels. As for the faith of prophets, it increases because the perfect accepts perfection, and it does not decrease. But it is objected that prophets experience a great unveiling at times, as on the night of the Mi'raj, so faith after it is not in the same station as before. And it is answered that this does not entail a disparity in their faith. Among what indicates that the faith of prophets increases is the statement of our master Ibrahim, peace be upon him and our Prophet: 'But that my heart may be at rest' [Al-Baqarah 260]. And in 'Mafatih al-Khazain al-'Aliyya' by Sayyidi Ali Wafa: the meaning of His saying 'Did you not believe?' is: Is your faith not sufficient? And he said: yes, but that my heart may be at rest from his restlessness at seeing the modality. And the meaning of what is reported in the Sahih: 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' is: that if doubt had occurred to him, it would occur to us all the more, considering the state of the ummah, not his state, or considering his state and it is humility. As for the faith of angels, it neither increases nor decreases, as the author mentioned in his 'Kabir' from Ibn al-Qayyim, and this is the well-known view; because their faith is innate by original nature, and what is innate does not vary. And Shaykh 'Abd al-Barr al-Ajhuri mentioned that the faith of angels increases and does not decrease, thus he made it like the faith of prophets, that they advance by [؟].
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the lines of the poem that deal with the increase and decrease of faith (iman). The commentator first explains that according to Ahl al-Sunnah, actions are part of the perfection of faith, so faith increases with increased obedience and decreases with decreased obedience. He clarifies that the majority of Ash'aris preponderate the view that faith increases, and this is what the poem indicates. Then he explains that the increase is caused by increased obedience (the 'ba' is causative, 'ma' is masdariyya). He then notes that while the general rule is that faith increases and decreases with deeds, Allah may also increase or decrease it by His sheer will without any external cause. Next, the commentator specifies that this increase and decrease applies to the faith of ordinary believers, not to prophets or angels. Prophets' faith only increases, because the perfect accepts more perfection, and it never decreases. He addresses an objection: the prophets experience great unveilings that might suggest a change in their faith. The answer is that this does not entail actual variation in the substance of their faith. He supports this with the example of Ibrahim (Abraham) asking to see how Allah revives the dead, which was not due to doubt but to seek tranquility of heart. He explains the hadith 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' as either referring to the state of the ummah or as an expression of humility from the Prophet. Finally, he discusses the faith of angels: the well-known view (from Ibn al-Qayyim) is that it neither increases nor decreases because it is innate (jibilli) and what is innate does not vary. However, a minority view (from al-Ajhuri) holds that angels' faith does increase, like that of prophets.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the primary cause for the increase of faith?
A) Divine will alone
B) Increase in human obedience
C) Increase in knowledge
D) The mere passage of time

Key Takeaway
Faith increases with obedience and decreases with disobedience, but Allah may also change it by His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a specific sin you committed recently. How did it affect your faith? Did you feel a distance from Allah? This lesson says faith decreases with disobedience. Are you willing to repent and rebuild your iman through obedience?
?
If Allah can increase or decrease your faith by His mere will, how often do you sincerely ask Him to increase your iman? Are you relying more on your deeds or on His mercy to keep your faith strong?
?
Examine your daily routine: what act of obedience did you perform today that genuinely strengthened your connection with Allah? If you cannot think of one, what will you do tomorrow to change that?
